## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as a function of population size P (density dependence) and possibly time t (environmental forcing, seasonality, or time-varying parameters). This is the standard setup for continuous-time population growth ODE models in ecology.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, density-independent per-capita rate)
- Time-varying intrinsic growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradual environmental trend affecting per-capita growth)
- Quadratic density dependence (logistic ODE / Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation, carrying capacity implied as ~1/c1)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (nonlinear strength/shape of density dependence)
- Gompertz-type (per-capita rate decreases with log P): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (multiplicative growth with logarithmic crowding)
- Richards generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) ** c3 (flexible sigmoid curvature and asymmetry)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low P plus crowding at high P)
- Linear harvesting (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (removal at constant rate independent of P)
- Proportional harvesting (effort-based): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to population size)
- Seasonal forcing of growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (periodic environment affecting births/deaths)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (resource base changes over time; denominator uses a time-dependent scale)
- Immigration/emigration plus growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (net constant influx/outflux term)
- Crowding-induced mortality as power law: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P ** c2 (births linear, deaths nonlinear with crowding)
- Per-capita rate as a rational function of P: dP_dt = P * (c0 - c1 * P) / (1 + c2 * P) (crowding saturates or mitigates via limiting factors)
- Delayed/implicit density feedback proxy (time-only forcing): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) * P (external forcing dominates; useful when density effects are weak)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density independence shows as dP_dt proportional to P (constant per-capita growth rate), whereas any curvature in dP_dt vs P suggests density dependence.
- Carrying capacity behavior corresponds to a stable positive equilibrium P* where dP_dt crosses zero with negative slope; typical forms include factors like (1 - c*P) or log(c/P).
- Allee effects are indicated by dP_dt < 0 at low P but > 0 at intermediate P (multiple equilibria), often requiring a multiplicative low-density factor such as (c*P - 1).
- Harvesting/exploitation introduces a negative term independent of P (constant yield) or proportional to P (effort-based), shifting equilibria and possibly causing extinction thresholds.
- Seasonality or recurring environmental variation appears as periodic dependence on t (sin/cos), producing oscillations in growth rate even when P is near equilibrium.
- Nonlinear crowding/mortality is suggested when growth turns down faster than quadratic (e.g., -P**c with c>2), reflecting stronger-than-logistic competition or disease spread effects.
- Time-varying environment or resource base implies parameters that change with t (e.g., c0 + c1*t or c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)), creating non-autonomous ODEs.
- If dP_dt depends weakly on P but strongly on t, the system may be driven by exogenous forcing (e.g., management actions, climate trend) rather than internal regulation.

Final search results
============================================================
Best expression     : P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4 + P + c5/P**5
Structure desc      : Additive model: cubic polynomial in P plus a small inverse-power correction c5·P^-5. Quadratic coefficients combine to (c1+c2)·P^2 ≈ 0.05535·P^2, and linear terms combine to (c3+c4+1)·P ≈ 0.2013·P, with cubic c0≈-0.00349. The reciprocal term (c5≈-0.0268) is negligible for moderate/large P but can dominate near P=0, acting as a sharp correction there. Approximate form: -0.00349·P^3 + 0.05535·P^2 + 0.2013·P - 0.0268/P^5.
Fitted params       : c0=-3.4880e-03, c1=4.9103e-01, c2=-4.3568e-01, c3=-2.8953e+00, c4=2.0966e+00, c5=-2.6828e-02
Train NMSE          : 4.96e-07
Test NMSE           : 4.60e-07
OOD Test NMSE       : 2.27e-04

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG13)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P + c6*P/(c7 + exp(-c8*(-c9 + P)))
Candidate formulas: 50

Let \(F_{\text{GT}}(P)\) denote the ground-truth function (note GT does **not** depend on \(t\)):

\[
F_{\text{GT}}(P)=0.2010739\;(-1+P/5.6365765)\,(1-P/10.2325613)\,P\;+\;0.2010739\,P\;+\;0.2010739\,\frac{P}{1+\exp\!\big(-5.6365765\,(P-0.6341847)\big)}.
\]

Key structural facts about GT:
- It is **not a polynomial**: it contains a **logistic** term \( \frac{P}{1+e^{-k(P-a)}}\).
- It has **no** \(1/P^5\), \((P+\text{const})^{-5}\), \(\log(\cdot)\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), or \(\exp(\alpha P)\) terms outside that logistic.
- It is **independent of \(t\)**.
- The first part expands to a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** plus the logistic term. So GT = (some cubic polynomial) + (logistic-in-\(P\) term).

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–7
1. \( \text{poly in }P + c5/P^5\). Even if \(c5=0\), it becomes a pure polynomial. GT is not a pure polynomial (has logistic). **No**.
2. Poly + \((c6|P|+1)^{-5}\) + \(c7/P^5\). Can zero those extra terms, but still only polynomial remains. **No**.
3. Same as 2 but \((Pc6+1)^{-5}\). Same issue. **No**.
4. Poly + \(c5(P^2c6+1)^{c7} + c8/P^5\). Can kill extra terms, still polynomial only. **No**.
5. Poly + \(c3/P^5\). Kill \(c3\) → polynomial only. **No**.
6. Poly + \((P+c3)^{-5} + c4/P^5\). Kill inverse-power terms → polynomial only. **No**.
7. Poly + \(c4/P^5\). Kill → polynomial only. **No**.

### Candidates 8–20 (rational/log/inverse-power variants)
8. Includes \(t\) term \(c3 t/(P+c4)^5\). To match GT (no \(t\)), must set \(c3=0\). Then it’s polynomial + \(c5/P^5\) → can set \(c5=0\) → polynomial only. **No**.
9. Has \(P\log(1+c4/P)\) and \(1/P^5\). To remove log must set \(c3=0\); remove \(1/P^5\) set \(c5=0\). Leaves polynomial only. **No**.
10. Same as 9 with \(\log(c4/|P|+1)\). Same conclusion. **No**.
11. Has \((c4\log(Pc5+1))^{c6}\). To remove must set \(c3=0\). Then polynomial + \(c7/P^5\) → kill \(c7\) → polynomial only. **No**.
12. Has \(\log(Pc4+1)/(P+c5)\) and inverse powers. To match GT must remove these by setting coefficients to 0, leaving polynomial only. **No**.
13–14. Poly plus inverse-power terms; can remove them, leaving polynomial only. **No**.
15. Pure polynomial + \(c4/P^5\). Kill \(c4\) → polynomial only. **No**.
16–17. Poly + \((c5|P|+1)^{-5}\) or \((Pc5+1)^{-5}\) + \(1/P^5\). Can remove extras → polynomial only. **No**.
18. Has \(P*c3/(P+c4)\) (a rational term). If \(c3=0\) it disappears; then polynomial + \(c5/P^5\) → polynomial only. If \(c3\neq 0\), GT has no such rational term. **No**.
19–20. Same pattern: removable inverse-power terms → polynomial only. **No**.

### Candidates 21–33 (exponentials, extra nonlinearities)
21. Poly + \(c5 e^{Pc6}\). GT’s non-polynomial part is logistic \(P/(1+e^{-k(P-a)})\), not a single exponential added. No choice of constants makes \(c5 e^{Pc6}\) equal that logistic term for all \(P\). **No**.
22. Poly + \((P+c3)^{-5} + c4/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
23. Contains \(t\) and \(P^{c3}e^{Pc5}\). Must kill \(t\)-term and exponential-power term to match GT’s lack of those forms, leaving polynomial only. **No**.
24. Poly + \(c4 e^{c5 t} + c6/P^5\). GT has no \(t\)-dependence; must set \(c4=0\). Then remove \(c6/P^5\) → polynomial only. **No**.
25. Has \(e^{Pc4}e^{c5 t}\) and \(t/(P+c7)^5\). Must kill both to remove \(t\) and exp-in-\(P\) terms → polynomial only. **No**.
26. Has \(P\log(c6/|P|+1)\) and \(1/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
27. Poly + \(c3/P^5 + c4/P^5\) (same type). Kill → polynomial only. **No**.
28. Poly + \(c3 e^{Pc4} + (P+c5)^{-5} + c6/P^5\). Must kill exp and inverse-power terms → polynomial only. **No**.
29. Poly + \(c5 (P^2 c6)^{c7} + c8/P^5\). Any nonzero \(c5\) gives a power-law term \(P^{2c7}\), not logistic. Kill → polynomial only. **No**.
30. Pure polynomial + \(c7/P^5\). Kill → polynomial only. **No**.
31. Pure polynomial + \(c4/P^5\). Kill → polynomial only. **No**.
32–33. Poly + \(P^{c5}c6 e^{Pc7}\) or \(P^{c5}c6 e^{c7|P|}\) + \(1/P^5\). These cannot equal a logistic term for all \(P\); killing them leaves polynomial only. **No**.

### Candidates 34–50 (more polynomials, inverse powers, \(t\)-dependence)
34. Polynomial + \((P+c7)^{-5} + c8/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
35. Polynomial + \(c5/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
36. Polynomial + \((P+c4)^{-5} + c5/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
37. Has \(e^{c4 t}/(P+c5)^5\) and \(t/(P+c6)^5\). Must set those coefficients to 0 to remove \(t\), leaving polynomial + \(c7/P^5\) → remove → polynomial only. **No**.
38. Poly + \(c5 e^{Pc6}\sin(c7 t+c8)\). GT has no \(t\); to remove \(t\) dependence must set \(c5=0\), leaving polynomial only. **No**.
39. Same as 22. Remove inverse-power terms → polynomial only. **No**.
40. Poly + \(c5 e^{c6 |P|^{c7}} + c8/P^5\). Not logistic; removing leaves polynomial only. **No**.
41. Poly + \(c3/(P+c4)^5 + c5/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
42. Has \(\exp(c4|Pc5|)\sin(c6 t+c7)\) + \(1/P^5\). Must kill to remove \(t\) dependence → polynomial only. **No**.
43. Has \(P*c4 e^{c5 t}\). Must set \(c4=0\) to remove \(t\), leaving polynomial + \(c6/P^5\) → polynomial only. **No**.
44. Polynomial + \(c3/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
45. Has \((c5+t)^{c6}\) and \((P+c7)^{-5}\). Must remove \(t\) dependence and inverse-power terms → polynomial only. **No**.
46. Polynomial + \(c3/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
47. Has \(t/(P+c4)^5\). Must set \(c3=0\) to remove \(t\), leaving polynomial + \(c5/P^5\) → polynomial only. **No**.
48. Polynomial + \(c7/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.
49. Polynomial + \(c3/P^5 + P^{-5}\). Even if \(c3=-1\) cancels \(P^{-5}\), still polynomial only. **No**.
50. Polynomial + \(c9/P^5\). Remove → polynomial only. **No**.

**Overall:** Every candidate is either (i) a polynomial in \(P\) plus removable nuisance terms like \(1/P^5\), \((P+\cdot)^{-5}\), logs, exponentials, or \(t\)-dependent pieces; or (ii) includes exponentials/sines/logs but not in the specific **logistic** form \(P/(1+\exp(-k(P-a)))\). None can reproduce the GT logistic term for all \(P\) by parameter choice.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG13)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P + c6*P/(c7 + exp(-c8*(-c9 + P)))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.201(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233)P + 0.201P + \frac{0.201P}{1 + \exp(-5.637(-0.634 + P))}$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) = -1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P^2/(5.637 \times 10.233)$$

So the first term times P:
$$0.201P\left(-1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P^2/57.68\right)$$
$$= 0.201(-P + P^2/10.233 + P^2/5.637 - P^3/57.68)$$

Combined with $0.201P$:
$$= 0.201(-P + P^2/10.233 + P^2/5.637 - P^3/57.68) + 0.201P$$
$$= 0.201P^2(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - 0.201P^3/57.68 + \frac{0.201P}{1 + \exp(-5.637(P - 0.634))}$$

So the GT has the form:
$$f(P) = aP^3 + bP^2 + \frac{cP}{1 + \exp(d(P - e))}$$

where $a < 0$, $b > 0$, and the sigmoid term is a key nonlinear component.

The **essential basis functions** are:
1. $P^3$ (cubic polynomial term)
2. $P^2$ (quadratic polynomial term)  
3. A **sigmoid-like** term: $\frac{P}{1 + \exp(-\alpha(P - \beta))}$

Note: there's no constant $P$ term remaining (the $-0.201P + 0.201P$ cancelled).

Now let me check each candidate against this structure. The key question is whether any candidate can reproduce the sigmoid term $\frac{cP}{1+\exp(-\alpha(P-\beta))}$.

The sigmoid function $\frac{1}{1+\exp(-\alpha(P-\beta))}$ is a fundamentally different basis function from:
- Polynomials ($P^n$)
- $1/P^5$
- $(P+c)^{-5}$
- $\log(1 + c/P)$
- $\exp(cP)$
- $1/(cP+1)^5$

None of these can exactly replicate a sigmoid. Let me verify this for each candidate type:

**Polynomial-only candidates** (1, 5, 7, 15, 27, 30, 31, 35, 44, 46, 48, 49, 50): These have only polynomial terms plus $1/P^5$. Cannot match sigmoid. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates with $t$ dependence** (8, 23, 25, 37, 38, 42, 43, 45, 47): Setting $t$-dependent coefficients to 0 reduces these to polynomial + other terms. Need to check remaining terms.

**Candidates with $(P+c)^{-5}$ or $(cP+1)^{-5}$** (2,3,6,13,14,16,17,19,20,22,28,34,36,39,41): These rational functions cannot replicate a sigmoid.

**Candidates with $\exp$** (21, 24, 28, 32, 33, 40): $\exp(cP)$ is not equivalent to sigmoid.

**Candidates with $\log$** (9, 10, 11, 12, 26): $P\cdot\log(1+c/P)$ is not a sigmoid.

**Candidate 18**: Has $P \cdot c_3/(P + c_4)$ which is a rational function, not sigmoid.

**Candidate 29**: Has $(P^2 c_6)^{c_7}$ which is a power function, not sigmoid.

After careful analysis, **none** of these candidates contain the sigmoid basis function $\frac{P}{1+\exp(-\alpha(P-\beta))}$ that is essential to the GT. No combination of the available basis functions (polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, power functions, rational functions) can exactly replicate a sigmoid for all $P$.
